<rate>3<//rate>< review>
Restaurant was comfortable, warm and rustic.  A few regulars enjoying their dinner.  Felt like I had walked into a Himalayan Cheers.

Had the chicken chow mein and chicken jhol momo.  The tomato chutney soup was spicey and tasty.  The momos were good when they were hot but were heavy dense hockey pucks of dough when they cooled off.  The chicken chow mein had dried left over tandori chicken pieces with light, chow mein noodles a little thicker than instant ramen.  It was greasy with hints of cilantro and green onions.  The chow mein looked good on Yelp but tasted like doctored up left overs.  Both were adorned with edible orchids.

The best part of the meal was the tomato chutney soup.  Meal was average and priced well with a Groupon coupon but not at regular full price.

If you want to have an inexpensive but satisfying chow mein, try King Dong.  Their chicken chow mein is delicious with fresh, succulent and juicy chicken and their noodles are a cross between Shanghai & hand pulled noodles for a third less.<//review>

Currently under new management.  Food was totally different and disappointing.  Service was terrible.  On a cold night, they insisted on keeping the doors open, so we had to freeze eating food that taste Indian rather than Nepalese.  I'm very sad that what was once a nice restaurant is gone forever.

Two years ago, I gave them 4 stars.  On my first of many times at this restaurant (under previous ownership), I quite enjoyed the evening. Food was good. Service was fine. Surrounding was cozy.

The lentil soup was delicious. The Nepalese bone-in goat curry was wonderfully complex, the palak paneer was served with nice creamy and tasty spinach and paneer cheese.

(Note that the food photos were from the good old days. Don't expect to see any of these any more.)

Unfortunately, none of these dishes are available any more.

So long and all the best to Himalayan Flavors.<//text>

<Text>Thing is, Himalayan Flavors has a lot of local competition. And against those competitors, it does not particularly shine.

The food was drastically under spiced to the point of being tasteless. The tofu was sour. How did that happen? I'm not sure, but it did.

<Response>None< /Response><Gmap_id>0x80857e963887556f:0x7329a2b67f5e4541<//Gmap_id></record>
</dataset><record>
<UserId.>114801170749519908100</UserId.>< Review>
Indo-Nepalese cuisine in a classy setting.

Parking: There is a lot next to the restaurant with several spots reserved for customers. Plenty of space on a weekend, though I went after noon.

Interior: Classy South Asian decor with some beautiful artwork around. The tables are largely geared towards smaller crowds with just a few for more than two people. There is also bar seating.

Service: Polite, but not the most responsive. I ran out of water several times despite coming in at an off-hour.

Food: A mix of North Indian with neighboring countries, such as Bhutanese and Nepalese. We had some of the traditional Indian restaurant food like the Chicken Tikka Masala and the Palak Paneer. Both dishes are good but not exceptional - rich in flavor, filling, appropriately spicy. Also had the datshi, a Bhutanese dish, for the first time. Interesting taste of spicy and sour mix of lentil and cauliflower. Unlike a lot of Indian dishes this one did not sit heavy in my stomach.

Price: Not the cheapest, but I've paid more for Indian food, felt the portion was worthwhile for what I paid. The restaurant also offers plenty of discount via Groupon and Yelp, check those out.

All in all, a good if not totally memorable place for a South Asian meal.</Review>

The very best PHO on Anaheim, possibly even all of long beach. This place it's very cozy, the service was fast and responsive to our needs. <Text>I'm so relieved that they are open during the pandemic! This pho place has always been my favorite pho in LA county. I have tried so many other places but nothing compares to this place. Everything from the customer service, to the tidiness, to the food is simply exquisite! I've been a recurring customer for roughly ten years and I have never been disappointed! To begin with, when we entered they warmly greeted us with a big smile. Also, the restaurant is always clean. The food is really good for such a cheap price. They are generous with their portions and meals. I used to order: chicken breast (ga Uc: g1) or (ga dui: g2). Sometimes, I either took rare steak (pho tai p2) or well-done flank (pho tai Chin P4). My family loves their spring rolls and combo fried rice. For the drinks. we took Thai tea and Iced coffee. i also appreciate their honesty. Over the years my family, my friends and I have the bad habits to forget many valuable items when we left the restaurant such as : Iphone, credit card, laptop, purses belonging to an expensive brand... They ran after us in order to return our missing belongings. We would've lost a good amount of valuable items if it weren't for their help! This place has a big parking, so check them out and you won't regret it! Additionally, they are doing dine-ins once again but with social distancing.</Text></record>

< Review>
New Pho has great Pho and a fantastic staff!
I am picky about my Pho so trust me when I say this place is great!
The broth is delicious and not watered down. They are super generous here with the meat, noodles and veggies (my favorite) so generous that if I had one complaint it would be that I would like more broth!
Prices are super affordable and fair. They accept credit cards and have a nice sized parking lot on the side where the entrance is actually located also another good thing about this spot is they do delivery through PostMates!
Definitely will be back again and recommend anyone in the area to try it if they are looking for genuine Pho.< /Review>

< review>
The bakery was very hip and French themed. Everything was clean looking and hip. I actually went two times, and the experience was different each time. First time was on a Friday afternoon, and all the breads and pastries were in stock. I went ahead and tried a bunch of different items and they were all quite good. One nice thing about it is that their "sweet" items were not overly sweet and definitely leaning more towards an Asian palette.

Their drinks were not bad, pretty normal and expected from any cafe/bakery with the usual array of coffee and espresso drinks, along some teas and Boba.

The second time I went was on a Sunday afternoon. The stock of bread was pretty low, and here in lies the problem. I'm not sure how often they're baking and keeping the shelves stocked as during my whole duration there (about 30 to 40 min or so as my group was hanging around and chatting), some items remained unavailable and empty the whole time.

Perhaps it's just opening pains. I hope it is, and as the employees get better at keeping up to pace with customer demand, it'll improve.

Another thing is that the drinks are often behind, and there's always people waiting for their orders to be called out. Depending on the employee the call outs are often very quiet too, so people not paying attention could wait for a while before noticing that their item is up.

Also, drinks are called and left on the counter. Receipts weren't really checked so if they call out a drink that others have, another customer could just walk up and nab it thinking its theirs.

Either way, I'm being more lenient as I think it's just usual growing pains for a new shop opening up.

Tl;dr: Bread and atmosphere is great, drinks are normal and ok. There are some improvements needed, but overtime kinks should (hopefully) be worked out.</review>

< Review>
Clairibel was a great server! The cooks were as accommodating as they could be to my food sensitivities, but they only can offer soy and gluten free for a *very small* amount of the dishes. While I appreciate that this is a vegan restaurant the food was not healthy, mostly soy, lots of gluten, sugary sauces etc. Overall the flavors were either bland or just confusing, my friends and I were pretty dissatisfied, especially for the price we paid... The furniture is also like patio furniture which I found strange. I think that this place definitely has potential but first and foremost needs to make some major menu changes. There are other meat substitutes that aren‚Äôt soy or gluten based and with more and more people developing these allergies the market for those meat substitutes is shrinking. The sugary sauces might mask the bland taste but it just didn‚Äôt work for me or my party. Everyone working there was very kind though, customer service was A+< /Review>

<Date>1574538051762< /Date><name>Jaklin Orlowski< /name><Review>Thrilled to have a new vegan restaurant in the area. Contemporary decor with a serene dine in setting. We ordered the fresh spring roles as am appetizer, Tom Yum tofu soup, eggplant and mushroom sauce baked in a clay pot, and a wide noodle dish. Four of us shared the above items, which are intended for a single serving, amongst 4 - not very big eaters - adults. It was plenty for dinner. Every single dish was delicious. Had dinner twice at Black Angus in the last 3 weeks.  Wish I could give it 5 stars but my first visit was horrible and the second was outstanding, so I gave them 4 stars.  First time was on a Sat, there were 6 in our party and restaurant was packed. Service and food coming out of kitchen was very, very slow--took more than 3+ hrs to complete dinner.  Our waitress came by shortly after we were seated and told us she would expedite our appetizer & drink orders first and would be back to get our entree orders next.  She disappeared and we couldn't flag a manager or another wait staff to assist us for over 30 minutes.  Heavy set manager was walking around with a tablet ignoring all customers and we couldn't get his attention eventhough I was waving at him like a lunatic.  Got so bad, I got up myself and found where the extra napkins, silverware, bread plates, takeout containers and bags were stored and helped myself.  After we completed our entrees, we had to wait an hour for dessert.  In contrast, my second visit was on a Tue and restaurant was only 25% full.  There were 4 in our party and the waitress was very attentive and professional.  We had to send a steak back because it was well done instead of rare and as soon as we showed her, she took it back immediately.  Even the same manager who ignored us in my first visit was walking the floor without his nose buried in a tablet.  If going to Black Angus on Fri or Sat evening, expect poor service and long waits.  Weekday evenings are probably your best options for this restaurant.< /Review>

We usually come when we get the coupon for the Campfire Feast for 2 because it's a fairly good deal. We usually get steaks, which are always good. I used to get the salmon because it was incredible! But about a year ago they decreased the size of the salmon fillet so now it's not really worth it. It still tastes good, normally. The food is good, the bartenders are very friendly and we usually don't have to wait too long to get a table. For dessert, we love the Sky High Mud Pie.

So why the 3 stars? They are ALWAYS understaffed on waiters. Once you're seated, it takes a while for your waiter to come because they only have 1, maybe 2 on a good night, people for a whole section. It's ridiculous and I feel bad for the waiters.

< Text>
I gave 2 stars for this restaurant for the following reasons.

Food is decent, nothing special, hasn't really changed in the last few years, so I give it 1 additional star from the lowest rating for maintaining food quality.

However, I have been here 4 times in the last 3 months and the food takes at least 25-45 minutes to come out. The waiters are also somewhat rude overall.

The 4th visit, the waiter interrupted me when I was assisting a relative with their order (he has me help when necessary due to a disability) and said "Stop. I'm talking to him, not you." First warning sign right there.

Next, since I didn't feel too hungry, I ordered an appetizer and concluded with "That's all, thanks". She asked "anything else?" To which I repeated "No that's all". She continued to insist and asked "No main dish?" And once again I refused. She asked a third time "Are you sure? The dishes are good." And at that point I was annoyed at her insistence and repeated "No. That's. All." once more through gritted teeth, enunciated nice and slow to make sure she heard it. To which she finally left.

Additionally, a minor inconvenience: the water cups sometimes have ice and sometimes are room temperature. I went with a party of 4 the last 4 times and it was usually a ratio of 1:3 or 2:2 with ice and room temperature, respectively. Weird, but it happened every time.

Tl;dr Decent food, slow service, somewhat rude, insistent, and interruptive attitude waiters. Request for ice water if you only get room temp water because you have around 50%-75% chance of getting room temp water.< /Text>

<Text>Never in my worst nightmares I thought I'd leave an unfinished steak. Black Angus Steakhouse: You need to learn how to do steak.

Let me start with how my expectations were rising up and then how finally went downhill in a hearth bit:

While doing business in the area I saw this place when I was driving around one day and then decided to give it a try for lunch. I got there at around 12:30 and the parking lot was full, so it gave me the hope that it would be a good place. I walked in and was told that the wait time was about 20 minutes. No problem so far since it makes sense that a place "that good" has similar wait times. I glanced at the menu and looked at the prices: This is a pricey place. "No problem", I though to my self, as of right now my expectations were really REALLY high considering all of the above.
I then was taken to my table, and ordered an item from the Dinner menu (not from the lunch menu though), the waitress said yes, that they served from that menu too at that time of the day. I went with the 18oz "certified angus beef" bone-in rib-eye, medium well.
I need to say that the food came out quickly and the service was great; I was given a piece of bread with butter and it tasted ok, as well as a Cesar salad that I had ordered. Here once again, so far so good.
Finally this beautiful steak came to the table: Juicy, perfectly cooked as requested, but the first unexpected warning sign came up: It was odorless... that's right, a freshly grilled steak not smelling like it... huh?...
I start eating this beauty and then, the disappointment: This steak was bland and totally flavorless! It was like a piece of meat that they had in the freezer and then got thrown to the grill after some expedited thawing process. The meat looked great to the eyes, but the mouth got really sad and dissapointed of this thing.
I can't convince myself that all of this wait and the long line of people waiting to enter are to eat this kind of food? I left my steak unfinished and ended up having the rest of the bread with butter, it was tastier than the meat...
Guys, seriously, you need to learn how to do steak.<//Text><Pics>None< /Pics><resp>None< /resp><GmapID>0x808fc8dec5b44ed5:0xa07622f75363e558</GmapID></record></dataset><record>
